function createCookie(name,value,days) {
	if (days) {
		var date = new Date();
		date.setTime(date.getTime()+(days*24*60*60*1000));
		var expires = "; expires="+date.toGMTString();
	}
	else var expires = "";
	document.cookie = name+"="+value+expires+"; path=/";
}

function readCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i < ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

}

This is the Main Gate located at Main St and Post St, Trainer.   (Clem Murray / Staff Photographer)  EDITORS NOTE:  SStress22-m   1/19/2012   Living &quot;down the bottom&quot; in southern Delaware County, the blue-collar towns on and near the river _ from Chester to Marcus Hook _ are no strangers to recession and hard times. But the projected March closing of the Conoco refinery that provided hundreds of well-paid jobs, the near bankruptcy of Chester-Upland schools, and the closing or merger of at least five area Catholic schools this spring, are creating harrowing levels of stress. Yvonne Vest, 60, a Conoco worker with four children in the Chester schools, never had high blood pressure. Now she does. Craig Galante, soon to be laid off from the refinery, will take a stab at opening a barber shop in Broomall. Seated in his union&acute;s hall in Marcus Hook for a briefing on severance, he predicted &quot;a ghost town between here and the state of Delaware&quot; when the last good jobs leave town. Faced with having to find a new job at 56, Michael Poissant, of Aston, will depend, at least for a while, on the income of his wife, a Crozier-Chester Hospital nurse. Widener professor Hal Shorey, a clinical psychologist with a practice in Chester, said, &quot;Hope is definitely at its low point here now.&quot; The psychological risk to a population when its goals are so consistently blocked, he said, is &quot;learned helplessness,&quot; which means &quot;you don&acute;t try to escape negative situations. You just sit there and take the negative hits because you don&acute;t believe there is anything you can do about it anyway.&quot;    13 of 15' />						</a>						</div>
